Shanghai Press Submits a Petition Requesting Remediation of Difficulties in Election Facts; Qu Shao Yi and Others Submit Two Points to the Central Government; Hoping That Both Law and Facts Are Taken Into Account 23

(Nanjing) For the National Assembly election, journalist associations in various places have successively elected candidates according to law. However, the organization of journalist associations and the number of members in various provinces and cities are clearly different. Therefore, journalist circles in places such as the capital Xijing and Hankou have already felt the practical difficulties and have successively requested remediation from the central government. Qu Shao Yi, Jiang Jianhou, Sun Menghua, Qian Hua, Xu Chihen, Jin Huating, Wu Zhongyi, Chen Wanli, Ma Chonggan, Guan Jiu'an, Sun Daosheng, Li Zutang, and other members of the executive and supervisory committees of the Shanghai Journalists Association have also jointly submitted a petition to the Central National Government and the General Election Office in their individual capacities, stating that the organization of journalist associations does not have fixed regulations like other free professional groups, and the acquisition of membership qualifications is not strictly limited. The proportion of associations and the difference in the number of members in various provinces and cities vary greatly. The exercise of the right to vote loses its balance, and the promotion of the election administration is difficult to be universal. Shanghai's press has the longest history of development and the widest scope of expansion, but the association only has more than 200 members. It has already elected candidates some days ago and should quietly wait for the central government to circle the candidates. However, it is deeply concerned that it will inevitably be unable to be elected due to the small number of members during the final election. Shanghai's press inherently represents the nature of the entire country, but according to natural trends, all candidates will inevitably be defeated, which cannot but be considered a regret. Moreover, other areas with relatively developed press are also feeling the same obstacles as Shanghai and have made more urgent appeals than Shanghai. This is the first request for remediation. Although the election of journalist representatives is not subject to regional control, according to the principles of election, all outstanding members of the national press who hold the center of gravity of the press must be given the opportunity to participate in order to live up to the expectations of the central government. Today, in important cities and culturally developed areas, many reporters are unable to exercise their right to vote because associations have not been established, and it has been difficult to count. Moreover, the capital is the political center, and the press has developed rapidly in recent years. It has also failed to establish an association and has not been able to elect candidates, which is even more insufficient to show fairness. This is the second request for remediation. As for how to remedy the situation, the central government naturally has the right to weigh the situation, but it hopes that both legal and factual circumstances will be taken into account, both to promote the success of the election administration and to comfort the expectations of the country. We respectfully offer our humble suggestions for consideration. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 22nd)

League of Nations Assembly in a Dilemma; Issue of Abyssinia's Attendance; Submitted to the World Court for Adjudication; Fierce Debate in the "Executioner" Committee; This Decision Controlled by Small Countries; Italian Delegation Hesitates After Hearing the News 28

(Geneva) The League of Nations Assembly continued its meeting this afternoon, electing Argentine representative Lamas as Chairman. The Abyssinian representative is temporarily attending as usual. The Credentials Committee announced that the issue of the credentials of the representatives of various countries has been postponed until next Tuesday for a decision. The Italian delegation is still absent. The delay in resolving the issue of credentials is due to the fact that the majority of small countries do not want to create a bad precedent on this issue, and it is possible that it will be rejected in the Assembly. Some have indicated that the committee may submit this issue to the Hague International Court of Justice for arbitration. In order to maintain its seat in the Assembly, the Abyssinian delegation submitted a memorandum to the League of Nations today, stating that 36 provinces in Abyssinia are still under the jurisdiction of the government established in the western Gohr region. (National Telegraph dispatch from the 21st)

(Geneva) It has been reliably learned that the Credentials Committee of the League of Nations Assembly discussed the Abyssinian issue today. The representatives debated fiercely. Finally, it was decided to submit the issue to the World Court. The committee met for a short time today. After a war of words, it was decided to appoint a subcommittee to study the matter and draft a report while waiting for the Hague Court's ruling. Before this, the Abyssinian representative Dr. Mardin had requested the Chairman of the committee, Peruvian representative Tudela, to allow him to attend and state his reasons.

Abyssinian Emperor Arrives in Geneva

(Geneva) The uncrowned Abyssinian Emperor arrived here at 5:35 PM yesterday, flying from Croydon Airport in London, intending to work with his delegation to fight for the right to attend the Assembly. The Abyssinian Emperor was warmly welcomed by the crowd upon disembarking, including hundreds of reporters and photographers, as well as 50 police officers who were there to provide protection. (Reuters dispatch from the 22nd)

(London) According to a press release issued by the Abyssinian Embassy in the UK, two-thirds of Abyssinian territory is still not controlled by Italian military force. Most of the 36 provinces of Abyssinia remain independent, have representatives, maintain contact with the central government in the west, and have all declared their allegiance to the Abyssinian Emperor. As for the Abyssinian army, it is now under the control of Grand Marshal Imru, who is stationed in the western city of Gohr, which is also the seat of the central government. (Havas dispatch from the 21st)

Continued League of Nations Assembly, Chairman Hopes for Cooperation Among Nations 29

(Geneva) Regarding the matter of the Abyssinian delegation attending the League of Nations General Assembly, a final decision has yet to be made. The Abyssinian Emperor has arrived from England and landed at the Cointrin Airport here at 5:35 PM today. The Abyssinian Chief Representative and Minister to the United Kingdom, Dr. Martin, welcomed him at the airport. A large crowd welcomed the Abyssinian Emperor. When the Abyssinian Emperor arrived in Geneva, the League of Nations General Assembly was in session electing a chairman. Argentine Foreign Minister Saavedra Lamas was elected chairman with 44 votes to 1. The dissenting vote was cast by Australian representative Bruce. There were also 4 abstentions.

Thereafter, Greek representative Politis, in the name of the Credentials Committee, submitted a report to the assembly, stating that out of the 52 member states attending the assembly, the credentials of 44 delegations had been reviewed and approved. The credentials of the other seven countries, as well as the Abyssinian delegation, still needed to be re-examined. Therefore, the assembly, based on Politis's recommendation, approved the credentials of the 44 delegations. As for the credentials of the Abyssinian representatives, a final decision would be made after the Credentials Committee submitted a second report. Until a final decision is made, the Abyssinian delegation may continue to attend the League of Nations General Assembly as usual. Therefore, the Italian delegation's attendance at the assembly will be delayed as a result. Italian officials are quite impatient. The Credentials Committee is now scheduled to reconvene tomorrow at 5 PM to discuss and make a decision as soon as possible. It has been confirmed that if the Abyssinian delegation is barred from the League of Nations General Assembly, the country has decided to file a lawsuit with the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague.

At 5:55 PM, Argentine Foreign Minister Saavedra Lamas took office as Chairman of the Assembly and, as is customary, delivered a speech. Saavedra Lamas first stated that the countries of South America have been working hard for world peace and have achieved remarkable results, as can be seen in the peaceful resolution of the Chaco War. He asserted that the League of Nations should address the issue of amending the Covenant with a calm and cautious attitude. As for the major countries that have not yet joined the League of Nations, efforts must be made to persuade them to cooperate with the League of Nations. This is undeniable, as the absence of these major countries from the League of Nations reduces its universality and weakens collective security. In conclusion, he stated that the League of Nations should be open-minded and accept criticism from all sides. He also stated that when the League of Nations was founded, all countries pledged to provide spiritual assistance to promote the common welfare and unity of all nations, even at the cost of some sacrifice. He now hopes that member states will uphold this spirit and cooperate to promote the development of the League's cause. After the Chairman's speech, the assembly was adjourned to reconvene at 10 AM tomorrow, and all delegations were asked to re-elect the Vice-Presidents and committee members of the assembly tomorrow morning. (Havas, 21st)

Results of Anglo-French Contacts, Disarmament Conference to Reopen, Suffering from Competitive Armaments, Germany Demands Close Attention 30

(London) According to a Times of London Paris correspondent, French Premier Blum and British Foreign Secretary Eden discussed important issues yesterday, including the reopening of disarmament negotiations. It is now believed that the British government is gradually proceeding with this matter in accordance with French suggestions. This is because: (1) Even the major countries engaged in the arms race are indeed showing signs of a willingness to rest due to the psychological and economic pressure caused by the competition; (2) Blum's recent success in easing communist attacks and resolving the dangerous labor unrest of textile workers has led to stability within France. French cabinet members now hope that a general European solution and the limitation of armaments will eventually lead to a reduction in armaments by addressing the matter from an economic rather than a political standpoint. The basic idea of Blum's new draft negotiations remains that, regardless of whether Germany joins or not, Germany's legitimate demands must be closely attended to. The intention is that once the agreement is completed, it should be submitted to Berlin with a condition that if Germany refuses to accept it, it would be tantamount to explicitly refusing to cooperate with other countries in Europe. The Hague Court May Not Rule During This Session, Committee Decides Assembly to Discuss Today 34

(Geneva) The League of Nations Credentials Committee held a closed-door meeting this morning and discussed the issue of Abyssinia's representative attending the General Assembly for two hours. It finally decided to propose to the General Assembly that a special procedure be adopted: since Italy has conquered Abyssinia and declared the establishment of the Italian Empire, it should seek the opinion of the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague on whether the credentials of the Abyssinian representative are still valid, in order to be cautious. The Committee also appointed a subcommittee of legal experts to study two issues this afternoon: (1) How to present this precise question to the Hague Court; (2) What impact this procedure will have in all respects, especially whether the Abyssinian representative should temporarily suspend their right to attend the General Assembly before the International Court of Justice makes a ruling.

The Credentials Committee's decision will naturally be submitted for discussion when the League of Nations General Assembly holds a public meeting tomorrow. League of Nations officials believe that whether the request for an advisory opinion from the International Court of Justice is made by the General Assembly or the Administrative Council, the Court may not be able to render a decision before the end of this session, no matter how quickly it handles the matter. In short, the only consequence of the Credentials Committee's decision is that the Italian representatives will not attend the General Assembly before the International Court of Justice expresses its opinion, and it is even possible that they will not attend until the end of this session. British Mediterranean, Naval Minister Hoare Returns Home After Observation, Explains Strengthening of Current Policy 35

(London) Naval Minister Sir Samuel Hoare, who recently toured the Mediterranean, returned to London today and issued the following statement: "Britain has no intention of abandoning its position in the Mediterranean and intends to find ways to deal with the various difficult problems that have recently arisen, and to make Britain's position even more secure in the future. This action by Britain is not intended to threaten anyone. It should be noted that we currently have no newly established Mediterranean policy. We will continue to maintain our original policy and maintain friendly relations with other countries to make the Mediterranean more stable and prevent our transportation from being affected. Although the air problem has changed the situation, it still cannot change our policy, but it will be slightly modified to suit the current situation." The area of Troodos on the island has the best summer resort, about 6,000 feet above sea level. The recent Italo-Abyssinian war has prompted the British to focus their attention on the situation in the Mediterranean and find ways to remedy its shortcomings. Hoare also explained the significance of this tour of the Mediterranean as follows: (1) To meet with the officers and sailors of the British fleet stationed there, because he did not want to learn about their work only from reports, but had to see it for himself; (2) To understand whether the lessons he had learned in the Mediterranean in the past twelve months were consistent with the facts. Japan's Tax Increase Plan Approved by Cabinet and Announced Yesterday; Increased Revenue to Implement National Policy 55

(Tokyo) As a result of the announcement today that the Japanese cabinet had approved the new tax plan of the Ministry of Finance, the market price of listed bonds on the stock exchange has fallen by one yen to six yen. According to this new tax plan, revenue for the next fiscal year will increase by 200,000,000 yen, and revenue for the following year will increase by 300,000,000 yen. The source of the aforementioned increase in revenue will be due to increased taxes on income, property, business profits, inheritance, domestic products, textiles, sugar, housing, stock exchanges, and other taxes. (Reuters dispatch, 22nd)

(Tokyo) The Minister of Finance, Baba Eiichi, stated the following in the form of a statement to thoroughly streamline the tax system:

This reform of the tax system, in terms of its significance and scale, will be a landmark event in the Japanese tax system. It will correct the imbalance in the national burden, directly and indirectly contribute to the stability of national life, and obtain a considerable degree of increase to strengthen finances and facilitate the implementation of several important national policies. The elasticity of the tax system has been deeply considered. In view of the current internal and external situation, this seems to be of great significance. Therefore, the national economy, which is the foundation of the tax system, will undergo rapid changes, and its purpose is of course not to hinder its development. The modern national expenditure must be the responsibility borne by all the modern citizens based on their ability, and it is hoped that it can contribute to the advancement of Japan's national destiny. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 22nd)

(Tokyo) According to the Ministry of Finance, the newly established tax items are five types, including house tax (transferred from local tax), property tax, sales tax, excise tax, and securities transfer tax. Among them, the tax items to be implemented from the 12th year are the sales tax, securities transfer tax, excise tax, and corporate tax in the property tax. As for the house tax and the individual tax in the property tax, the investigation of rent revision, property evaluation, etc. will take about one year, so it is scheduled to be implemented in the 13th year. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 22nd)

(Tokyo) The net revenue of the national treasury for this tax system streamlining plan is 200 million yen in the first year and 300 million yen in each subsequent year. Compared with the original plan of the Tax Bureau, it has been considerably reduced. However, the national treasury taxation is thus obviously eased. According to the unreleased revenue from the reform of the customs tax system, there will be an increase of about 30 million yen. In addition, the reduction of the local tax burden in the national treasury increase is about 220 million yen in the first year. Therefore, if the national tax increase from this tax system reform is comprehensively considered, it will nominally be about 450 million yen in the first year and about 500 million yen in ordinary years. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 22nd)

The opening exchange rate between British and American currencies was $5.063125, which was 0.03125 higher than yesterday's closing rate. One hour later, it continued to rise 0.0125 to $5.064375. This price did not change until 1:00 PM.

British-French The opening exchange rate of the French currency was 76.91, which was one pound higher than yesterday. One hour later, it rose another two pounds and then remained unchanged.

Securities

New York The securities market continued to be mixed this morning. Securities prices mostly fell due to profit-taking. However, steel stocks and oil stocks are expected to rise. The announcement by President Roosevelt regarding the meeting on September 30 to discuss the joint venture of electric power industry groups seems to have temporarily stopped its impact on public utility stocks. Some quarters expect the market price to rebound. Commercial news is good, and general sentiment leans towards bullish. The current stock market prices in New York are listed on the left.

Liverpool Wheat The opening was quiet and lacked any new features that could arouse interest. The market price fell under the pressure of normal profit-taking, but the market situation stabilized slightly after the price fell. At 1:00 PM, the October price was 7 shillings and ten and a half pence, which was one penny lower than yesterday's closing price. Liverpool Cotton The cotton market was quiet today. At 1:00 PM, the October price fell by three pounds to 6.41.

New York Cotton The opening this morning was stagnant. The December price was unchanged and remained at 11.80. It then fell by two pounds, but the trend was upward, so the price at noon was four pounds higher than yesterday's closing price at 11.84.

Chicago Wheat There was not much change this morning. The December opening fell slightly. The noon price was 113.625, which was 0.125 lower than Monday's closing price. The Department of Agriculture has released its wheat production estimate for this year, stating that 37 wheat-producing countries, excluding Russia and China, produced a total of 2,938,000,000 bushels, a decrease of 5% compared to the previous year. Grain also fell at the opening. The December price fell 0.375 to 94.25. It continued to fall before noon, and the noon price was 93.875, which was 0.875 lower than yesterday.

Gao Bandit Gang Splitting Up and Fleeing; Traces of Bandits in Four Counties: Huanggang, Huangpi, Huang'an, and Macheng. Garrison Troops and Security Regiments Begin Joint Suppression. 59

Hankou Correspondence: The bandits under Gao Junting in eastern Hubei are repeatedly disturbing various counties, and the people are suffering greatly. Although the central government has dispatched a large army to jointly suppress them with the security forces of various counties, they have been unable to completely eliminate them as they are suppressed in one place and then flee to another. Recently, Pacification Director He Chengjun and Provincial Chairman Yang Yongtai convened a border area suppression meeting to determine strategies. Chairman Chiang also telegraphed Commander-in-Chief Wei Lihuang, who was in the Wei area, stating that before he returns to his defense area, Director He should supervise the suppression of the remnants of this bandit gang. Recently, it has been reported that the remnants of the bandits have split up and fled in the four counties of Huanggang, Huangpi, Huang'an, and Macheng in eastern Hubei. One group of more than 600 people fled from Shangcheng to the Yantian River and Xiongjia Ao areas of Macheng County. Another group of more than 300 people fled from Daqishan in Huanggang County to the Gunzi River and Baifusi areas northeast of Tuanfeng County. Another group of more than 400 people passed through the borders of Huangpi and Huang'an counties and fled to the Sandian Street area of Huanggang County. Another group of more than 200 people fled from Fujianchang River to Chengmagang and Yangliutang in Macheng County. Another group of more than 100 people fled from Lingyun Temple in Fuzhou to the Qiliping and Tiantai Mountain areas in Huang'an County. Another group of more than 700 people occupied the Daxiaojiulong Mountain, Wuyue Mountain, and Daxiaowushan areas of Liluo County. Recently, the bandits spreading in Huanggang County have become quite rampant. According to information from Dongsan, Xinzhou, Cangbu, Liji, Yangluo, Weijiazui, and Zhujiaji have either become bandit dens or are frightened several times a night. Yesterday, people from Wuhan gathered to discuss the situation. In addition to petitioning the military authorities to dispatch more capable troops for suppression, they also plan to establish a Rural Clearing Committee to assist in the operation. It is reported that the units of Wei Lihuang and Liang Guanying, as well as the security regiment of Ding Bingquan, have now begun joint suppression, and it is expected that the area can be cleared soon. (September 21)

Zhang Jia'ao Arrives in Guangzhou to Finalize Plans for Building a Huangpu Branch Line; Route to Run from Xicun via Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway to Yuzhu; Total Cost Including Port Development Fee Is 10 Million Yuan 60

Guangzhou Correspondence: The situation in the Southwest has recently been peacefully resolved, and the central authorities are taking the opportunity to develop transportation and promote economic construction. Of these economic construction projects, nothing is more important than the development of Huangpu Port and the construction of a branch line of the Yuehan Railway. Premier Chiang telephoned Railway Minister Zhang Jia'ao at the beginning of the month, summoning him to Guangzhou to discuss various ongoing projects. Zhang arrived in Guangzhou on the morning of the 10th of the month on the Yuehan Railway train. Those who came with him included Deng Yiguang, Director of the Chengyu Railway Bureau, Hou Jiayuan, Director of the Xiangmo Railway Bureau, Ling Hongxun, Director of the Yuehan Railway Bureau, Xie Fencheng, Chief of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Railways, and a total of 15 secretaries and specialists. Zhang went to Huangpu on the same day to meet with Premier Chiang, reporting on the general situation of his inspection of railway affairs along the way. On the 12th, Premier Chiang summoned Minister Zhang, the directors of various railway bureaus, and Guangzhou Mayor Zeng Yangfu at the Huangpu Executive Office. In addition to Minister Zhang, those who attended that day included Ling Hongxun, Li Luchao, Wang Renkang, Li Xiangen, and the directors of various railway bureaus. During the meeting, Premier Chiang inquired about the recent situation of various railways in the country. He then thoroughly discussed the construction of the Huangpu branch line of the Yuehan Railway and the development of Huangpu Commercial Port. Subsequently, Zeng Yangfu presented the plans for the development of Huangpu Port, and Ling Hongxun presented the engineering plan for the Huangpu branch line to Premier Chiang for review. A plan was immediately agreed upon, and it was decided to start construction in the near future. Funds would also be allocated by the central government. The meeting ended at 2:00 PM that day. On the same day, Minister Zhang, accompanied by Ling Hongxun, Wang Renkang, Li Luchao, Hou Jiayuan, Xie Fencheng, and others, went to Huangpu to survey the area and measure the construction of the branch line from the Yuehan Railway to Huangpu. On the 13th, Zhang also sent personnel to inspect railway affairs on the Guangzhou-Sanshui Railway. On the 14th, he inspected the road administration on the Chinese section of the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway with Li Luchao. Zeng Yangfu was appointed by the Ministry of Railways in conjunction with the Guangdong Provincial Government as the supervisor of the Huangpu Port development. The appointment was then proposed by Chairman Huang and passed at the ninth meeting of the Guangdong Provincial Government on the 15th. After all matters were completed, Minister Zhang left Guangzhou at about 1:00 PM on the afternoon of the 17th, taking the Guangzhou-Kowloon train to Hong Kong to await a ship to return north. According to Minister Zhang, concrete plans have been drawn up for the development of Huangpu Port and the construction of a branch line of the Yuehan Railway. The project is scheduled to be completed in the winter of next year. The cost of building the road and constructing the wharf and warehouse is estimated at 10 million yuan. Furthermore, an investigation has revealed that the Huangpu branch line has a significant relationship with commerce in South China. According to information from the Railway Bureau, the Huangpu branch line of the Yuehan Railway starts at the Xicun Station in Guangzhou, passes through the suburbs of Guangzhou, and intersects with the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway in Dongshan. It then follows the Zhongshan Highway directly to the Yuzhu Market in Huangpu as its terminus. The branch line is a total of 40 Chinese miles long. The allocation of construction costs is as follows: 2 million yuan for the construction of the tracks, 1.5 million yuan for the construction of the stopping stations and the filling of the wharves, and 5 million yuan for the port development project, which will start with the construction of wharves and roads, followed by the construction of warehouses in the second phase. The total cost will reach 10 million yuan. The funds will be allocated by the National Economic Commission. If there are no obstacles, construction can begin around October of this month.

Songjiang, Theft Cases Occur Frequently in the Countryside 61

The family of Xia Shengtang, a resident of Xiahengjing Township in the county, is moderately well-off and has long been coveted by thieves. Yesterday (21st), a group of thieves speaking in a strong Hakka accent and carrying pistols broke into his house and robbed it. They then went to the home of Zhu Guihe in Qiangang Township in the same area to rob. The losses of both families were more than 100 yuan each. The victims have reported the cases to the police bureau and requested an investigation.

Since Chen Ziqiang, a technician from the Jiangsu Provincial Land Administration Bureau, was appointed as the team leader of the Kunshan County survey, the work has been carried out actively. The topographical and traverse surveys have been completed one after another, and the household survey has also been completed and is currently being inspected, and the indoor work is being done.

Jiading, Soil Paste Manager Fined Heavily 63

Gao Baocun, the manager of the Sanxin Soil Paste Company, was deemed by the Provincial Committee to have raised the selling price of soil paste and has been detained for a long time in the Songjiang Inspectorate and the local county government. The county government has now sentenced him to a fine of 18,000 yuan. Gao does not accept the decision and is preparing to appeal. He has been granted permission to be temporarily released on bail during the appeal period. He was released on the 17th on bail provided by the Naxiang Wankang Sauce Garden and the Chenxinchang Clothing Store in the city.

Suzhou More Judicial Officials Appointed 64

Lin Xueming, the presiding judge of the Second Civil Tribunal of the Jiangsu High Court, was transferred by order of the Ministry to serve as the Chief Prosecutor of the Nantong District Court. The vacancy was filled by Zhu Zongzhou, the presiding judge of the Fourth Branch of the High Court. Zhu's vacancy was filled by Zheng Shikang, a judge of the same court, who was promoted. Furthermore, Liu Shizhu, the prosecutor of the Nantong District Court, was appointed by order to serve as a judge of the Fourth Branch of the High Court. Xiong Zhaowei, the chief clerk of the Jiangdu District Court, is acting as the clerk of the Shanghai District Court. The vacancy will be filled by Zhang Bingheng. Mu Liangxu is acting as the clerk of the Wuxi District Court and is temporarily working at the High Court. Additionally, Zhang Mian, a county officer of Taixian County, has been appointed to another position by order of the Ministry, and the vacancy will be filled by Jiang Youhua.

Soil Smuggler Escorted to Province for Interrogation 65

The notorious soil smuggler Guo Ruzhao (also known as Guo Chunqing) was previously wanted by the Provincial Garrison Headquarters for a case involving smuggling private soil. Earlier this month, Guo was arrested by police officers from the Second and Third Precincts of the Public Security Bureau near the Yuanmiao Temple, Niujiao Hong. After being interrogated by the County Government following the Public Security Bureau's transfer, it was deemed that the case involved a fugitive wanted by the Provincial Garrison Headquarters. Therefore, yesterday morning (the 22nd), detectives from the Public Security Bureau's Investigation Team were ordered to escort the suspect to the province for investigation and prosecution.

Tragic Death by Self-Inflicted Axe Wound 66

Liu Linhe, a 22-year-old butcher's apprentice from Wuxi working at the Shunji Meat Shop outside the Changmen West Jin Bridge, suddenly grabbed a large meat cleaver and chopped his neck at around 4 PM the day before yesterday (the 21st), severing his trachea. He bled profusely on the spot, immediately collapsing and dying. The scene was extremely gruesome. Yesterday (the 22nd) afternoon, a member of the District Court was dispatched to examine the body. As for the reason for his suicide, one theory is that the shop owner, Zou Hubao, falsely accused him of theft. However, according to the shop owner's statement, the deceased suffered from a mental illness. It is unknown which of the two accounts is accurate.

Wuxi Coppersmith Beats Rickshaw Puller to Death 67

Zong Xiaosizi, a 26-year-old from Yancheng residing at No. 8, Jia 11, Bao 4, Lihua Town, outside the North Gate of this county, worked as a rickshaw puller and was unmarried. He had five brothers, and his father was deceased. His mother, Madam Li, is 58 years old and still alive. Around 7 PM the night before last, Xiaosizi was pulling a fashionable young woman towards Zhoushanbang from the Jixiang Bridge area. Unexpectedly, while passing the entrance of Mengyuan Alley on the road, he happened upon Lian Lingen, a coppersmith from the Dongyou Temple Bridge Craft Machinery Iron Factory, and several others, who had just finished a celebratory banquet at the Da Zhonghua Restaurant (for the wedding of Chen Zifan, the factory's pattern-making director). They were lingering on the road, and the rickshaw puller accidentally bumped into Lingen with the rickshaw's shaft. Lingen became enraged and slapped Xiaosizi several times in the face. He then repeatedly punched him and struck his vital points, and finally delivered a fierce kick, causing him to immediately fall to the ground, his face turning pale, and losing consciousness. After police officers Chen Feilong and Shi Xuesheng from the Third and Fourth Precincts heard the news and arrived, they arrested the assailant Lian Lingen and took him to the station. They also sent the injured Zong Xiaosizi to the Puren Hospital branch clinic for treatment, but due to severe internal injuries to his stomach, intestines, and heart, he could not be saved and died immediately. Yesterday (the 22nd) at 9 AM, Xi Zhongliang, the head of Tian San Tu, reported the incident to the District Court and requested an inquest. At 2 PM in the afternoon, Prosecutor Shen and Coroner Wang went to conduct the inquest. They found a fatal punch wound on the deceased's chest and his testicles were also crushed by the kick. He also had minor injuries on his hands and feet. It was determined that the death was due to the injuries. They then instructed the deceased's mother to prepare the body for burial, pending further investigation.

Widening the North Gate Street 68

The section of North Main Street in this county is a hub of commerce, but unfortunately, the narrow street impedes traffic and inconveniences pedestrians, greatly affecting business. The Construction Bureau planned to widen it this year, but due to a lack of funds, it could not be implemented. However, local merchants, recognizing the critical relationship between transportation and commerce, proposed voluntarily donating funds to request the widening. More than thirty businesses, including the Jiusheng Silk Shop inside the North Gate, submitted a petition to the Construction Bureau requesting that the section from the North Gate to the Shuyuan Alley be widened first, without demolishing the North Gate Yuecheng. After Director Zhang submitted the petition, in addition to subtly inquiring about the opinions of various parties, he also reported the information to the County Government for verification. The County Government will now convene a County Construction Committee meeting to discuss and decide. Considering this, the widening of the North Gate Street should not be far off.

Mao Yijun Arrested in Yangzhou 69

Mao Yijun, the former director of the Third Precinct of the Public Security Bureau in this county, and Sun Zhongjie, a member of the bureau, were involved in a case of embezzlement of fines, leading to mutual accusations. Initially, the court detained Sun, and Mao was released on a written guarantee of two thousand yuan pending judgment. Li Zhigang, a small owner from Yongmao Ti Zhuang, was responsible for guaranteeing Mao's release. Subsequently, the court sentenced Mao to a fine of three hundred yuan and one year of imprisonment. Mao refused to accept the judgment and appealed to the Supreme Court, which upheld the original judgment. Afterwards, the court in this county repeatedly summoned Mao to appear in court for execution of the sentence. However, Mao, having already been dismissed from his position, went into hiding. The court then summoned and detained the guarantor, Li Zhigang, before releasing him on a written guarantee of ten thousand yuan last month, ordering him to deliver Mao for execution. Li then learned that Mao was hiding in Yangzhou and went there to search for him. He finally found Mao on the 19th of this month, turned him over to the Jiangdu District Court for detention. Li then returned to Wuxi yesterday to report to the Wuxi court. After being interrogated by Prosecutor Ren, he was ordered to return and await the dispatch of police to escort Mao from Yangzhou for investigation and prosecution.

Changzhou Autumn Cocoon Market Sees Increased Supply 70

The Wuyi autumn cocoon market has been open for three or four days, but due to the relatively low prices, it has not been very active. In the past two days, cocoon businesses in various townships have increased prices, resulting in an increase in supply. The Jiang Henghe and Jiu Hua businesses in Hutang Bridge in the southern countryside are receiving more than thirty loads of cocoons per day, with prices ranging from thirty-four to thirty-five yuan. The Tailong, Fuchang, and Xie Tongyi businesses in Qishuyan are receiving more than twenty bundles or ten ancestral units of cocoons per day, with prices ranging from thirty-two to thirty-three yuan, slightly lower than the prices in the southern countryside, resulting in fewer cocoons received.

Yan Xiaolan Passes Away in Changzhou 71

Mr. Yan Xiaolan, a scholar from Wuxi, was erudite and talented, and his works, such as the Tongjiang Fishing Terrace Collection, have long been well-known. On the 20th, he accompanied Zhao Xuenan from Suzhou to Changzhou to visit Mr. Qian Mingshan. Qian hosted them at the Luyang Restaurant. Before the meal was finished, Mr. Yan suddenly complained of dizziness and began to stagger. He was quickly supported, but he was already unable to speak. A telegram was immediately sent to the Wujin Hospital requesting that someone be sent to pick him up. He was given acupuncture treatment, but he succumbed to a stroke and passed away. A telegram was sent to his family, and a coffin was brought to Changzhou on the 21st for the viewing.

Changshu Fire at Pawnshop Kills Cook 72

The Dalu Pharmacy on Temple Street was completely destroyed by fire in the early morning of the 21st, and an apprentice from Shaoxing who was studying there was burned to death. The shop telegraphed his family in Shanghai, who came to Changshu to arrange the funeral. Unexpectedly, that evening, a fire also broke out at the Yonglong Pawnshop on South Main Street, also killing a 65-year-old shop clerk, a situation even more tragic. It is customary for pawnshops here not to light lamps at night, but to go to sleep after dark to avoid accidents. The Yonglong Pawnshop had a cook named Xu Er, 65 years old, who had been employed for more than ten years. Last night (the 21st), Xu followed his usual routine of feeling his way to the upper floor after dinner to go to bed. However, he always had to smoke several pipes of dry tobacco before sleeping. At around 8 PM, a fire suddenly broke out on the upper floor. Those who heard the alarm rushed to the rescue. Fortunately, it was still early, and the fire was extinguished after a short time, destroying one building upstairs and downstairs. However, Xu Er was suddenly discovered to be missing. While searching for him, the body of Xu Er was found by the Zhendong Fire Brigade in the rubble, his head and face charred beyond recognition, a truly tragic sight. According to the shop's employees, Xu Er was old, deaf, and blind. When the fire broke out, he was unable to escape and was burned to death.

Nantong New Cotton from Nantong Listed 73

Nantong's new cotton crop is bountiful this year, although the situation in the coastal reclamation areas is worse. Cotton businesses in urban and rural areas all opened for trading on the 20th, with a large supply available. Dasheng Textile Factory and manufacturers from Shanghai, Wuxi, and other places, as well as local cotton merchants, are competing to purchase the crop. The price of raw cotton is 47 yuan per picul. It is estimated that this year's cotton production in the Nantong and Yancheng areas will yield 1.2 million piculs of raw cotton.

Linzhun Rewarding and Punishing Short-Term School Principals 74

Fengyang County previously compiled and forwarded the performance reports of the principals of various short-term primary schools for the 24th year of the Republic to the provincial government for evaluation. It has now been heard that the assessment has been completed, and the county government has been instructed to reward and punish them accordingly. Qu Shaoshun, Shi Maoxuan, and Geng Yubing were commended, and Liu Zian, Sun Weilin, and Shi Zhenqiu received bonuses. Qiu Liang was admonished, and Wang Mingsu, Zhang Zijiu, Hu Deyi, and Bi Wenchang were given demerits. Those who received demerits should also be sponsored by the county to study at the Fengyang Provincial Normal Simple Normal Department at the beginning of the first semester of this year, and their vacant positions should be filled by others.

Ningbo Cholera Rampant in Eastern Xiangshan 75

It has recently been discovered that cholera is rampant in the eastern countryside of Xiangshan, especially in the townships of Wujing, Xihan, and Linguan. It is spreading rapidly, and those who contract it die quickly. In the villages of Ma'ao and Shengjia alone, the death toll has already reached thirty or forty people. Furthermore, Eastern Xiangshan is located in a remote rural area and has no hospitals, so when an acute epidemic occurs, patients have no choice but to await death. The residents of the area are now eagerly hoping that the authorities will find ways to provide relief.

Bengbu Seizure of Large Quantity of Smuggled Paper 76

Since the establishment of the anti-smuggling inspection office stationed in Bengbu by the customs to prevent smuggling via roads, the authorities' earnest crackdown on smuggled goods has slightly curbed the practice of smuggling. Recently, more smuggled paper has been seized on the river's surface. At 12 PM on the 19th, personnel from the Changhuai River Police Bureau's river inspection station spotted a people's boat carrying bamboo rafts, arriving from downstream, loaded with thirteen bundles of large paper and forty-five bundles of wood pulp paper. It was found that they were transported from Zhenjiang but had no customs tax certificate. The customs inspection office was notified and the boat, paper, and boatmen were all detained and reported to the head office for handling.

Solemn and Tragic "September 18th" Memorial Meeting 77

...Jointly Held by Various Schools in Beiping... (Special Dispatch from Beiping)

In view of the successive outbreaks of the Chengdu and Beihai incidents, the Beiping authorities had already issued clear orders regarding the precautions for "September 18th." Moreover, Beiping has a special status and a large concentration of foreigners. If given the opportunity, the other side could take advantage of it to create disputes similar to the above two incidents in order to achieve certain special purposes. Therefore, the various authorities here were particularly apprehensive and fearful on the fifth anniversary of "September 18th." On that day, in addition to dispatching a large number of soldiers and police to be stationed at various schools and strictly prohibiting outdoor marches, soldiers and police were also deployed at all main thoroughfares in the city to prevent unforeseen events. Most noteworthy was the fact that heavily armed soldiers and police were stationed near the residences of people from "friendly nations," as if facing a formidable enemy, providing meticulous protection and strict security. All of our compatriots seem to need to reflect on the bitter and spicy flavors in this. The reporter went out to patrol at six o'clock in the morning and did not return until eight o'clock in the evening. Although shocking scenes were everywhere, the whole city passed through safely without any disputes. Students from various schools also conducted their solemn memories under heavy and tragic atmosphere, with no other action. In addition to a few schools holding memorial meetings on campus, around 3 PM in the afternoon, all major, middle, and primary schools in the city, in a joint effort with a certain college in Jiaodao, Duanwangfu, held a memorial meeting. This was the only memorial meeting in Beiping that day worth recording. The following is a brief account of the situation before and after.

(1) Before the Meeting Upon entering the area near Jiaodao, Duanwangfu, one immediately felt a serious atmosphere, making one want to flee. Upon closer inspection, it was found that this was due to the dense presence of soldiers and police, detectives moving back and forth like shuttles, and the glittering bayonets reflecting the sun. The situation was particularly serious in front of the gate of a certain college, where the meeting was held. However, the reporter observed that representatives from various schools, as well as male and female students who voluntarily participated, came in an endless stream from all directions. Worthy of particular note was their attitude, which was neither dejected and dispirited, with furrowed brows, nor agitated and impulsive, excitedly moving forward, but rather a kind of air of normality, yet also as if they recognized their own mission and bravely advanced. Their attitude was truly awe-inspiring.

Around 3 PM, the total number of representatives from various schools and students who volunteered to participate was more than 600. Professor Tao Xisheng, who was scheduled to deliver a speech, was unable to attend due to a temporary reason. Those who did attend were Zhang Dongsun and Wu Juexian, as well as a certain gentleman who had recently arrived in Beiping from the Northeast Volunteer Army, who had come to participate, attracting attention. In the half hour before the meeting, military and police personnel, seeing that the participants were quite enthusiastic, feared that unexpected incidents might occur during the meeting and attempted to prevent it from taking place. Fortunately, a certain president of the college did his utmost to vouch for the meeting to the military and police personnel. It was heard that the military and police personnel questioned the president, saying, "If any accidents happen, who will be responsible?" The president replied, "I will be solely responsible." Therefore, the fact that the memorial meeting was able to take place was also due to the sympathy and assistance of the president. Compared to the president of a certain normal school in the neighborhood, who tightly closed the school gate on the evening of the 17th and invited a large number of soldiers and police to stand guard with guns inside the iron fence gate, prepared to act at any moment, their virtue and wickedness cannot be measured by miles.

(2) At the Meeting The meeting was held in the auditorium of a certain college. At the entrance, there was a white cloth banner with the nine characters "Fifth Anniversary of the September 18th Memorial Meeting." Upon entering the meeting place, the first thing that caught the eye were five large charcoal drawings hanging on the wall, all depicting the actual situation related to the "September 18th" Incident. The names of the five paintings were as follows: (1) After "September 18th," Northeast compatriots crowded and fled into the customs. When will we "fight back to our old home"? (2) Japanese cavalry entered Shenyang city as if entering an unpopulated area. (3) On "September 18th" of the 20th year, the Japanese in Shenyang city shattered the Chinese people's dreams. (The reporter noted that the various phenomena depicted in this painting were extremely thought-provoking, such as "Overnight, Japanese residents have all turned into soldiers," etc., all of which were extremely alarming.) (4) Among the people who fled back from the Northeast, children asked their mothers, "When will we go home?" (5) The Volunteer Army struggling to resist. All of the paintings were extremely vivid and powerful, and the brushstrokes were very mature, presumably produced by someone with a very deep cultivation of this situation.

A few minutes before the meeting, a male student and two female students from a certain civilian school voluntarily sang songs such as "Fight Back to Our Old Home" and "National Salvation March" in the crowd under the gaze of the public. The tones were mature and the aura was majestic. At first, the reporter thought that it came from the mouths of many adults, but upon closer inspection, it was found that it was just a young boy and two girls, around twelve or thirteen years old, with ragged clothes and insufficient nutrition. The reporter was astonished and admired them immensely.

The procedure of the memorial meeting was extremely simple. After the chairman's report, a certain gentleman who had just arrived in Beiping from the Northeast Volunteer Army was invited to the stage to report. This gentleman's face was haggard, but his spirit was exceptionally high-spirited. It was evident that he was a patriotic person engaged in arduous struggle. He took the stage amidst warm applause and reported in detail on the current situation of the Northeast Volunteer Army. Many things were not easily known to outsiders. The reporter recorded the main points as follows:

The Volunteer Army is currently located everywhere in the four northeastern provinces (Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Jehol). It is now divided into fifteen armies and fourteen guerrilla teams. Among the fifteen armies, eight are called the "Northeast People's Revolutionary Army," led by Wang Degong, Zhao Shangzhi, and others. Seven armies are called the "Northeast Anti-Japanese Allied Army." In terms of region, they are divided into five military districts: (1) Liaoning District, (2) Jilin District, (3) Harbin District, (4) Heilongjiang District, and (5) Jehol District. Since this year, the five districts have totaled more than 100 battles with the Japanese-Manchu side in May, with the Volunteer Army numbering more than 11,000 people. In June, there were a total of 270 battles, with the number of people exceeding 12,000. In July, there were 250 battles, with a total of more than 17,000 people. In August, there were 230 battles, with a total of more than 16,000 people. In terms of organization, although there are titles such as commander, everything is elected by everyone. There is only responsibility and no rights. If there is dereliction of duty, everyone jointly decides. The current Northeast Volunteer Army has merged with the people, helping the people to harvest or cultivate, and the people also help them fight against the Japanese-Manchu army. Since Japan implemented the confiscation of civilian firearms, the merging of villages, and the strict implementation of entry and exit permits, the people's resentment towards them has deepened. Now there are two major opposing camps, one being the Japanese-Manchu army and the other being the entire population of the Northeast (that is, the Volunteer Army). Under this situation, the people of the Northeast can only choose between joining the Volunteer Army and being trampled to death by the Japanese-Manchu. The two paths of living in peace and fleeing into the customs are now completely impossible. The Volunteer Army fights the Japanese-Manchu army entirely by guerrilla warfare, which reduces the power of many new Japanese weapons. This is also why the Volunteer Army has been able to struggle to this day. The troops of the puppet "Manchukuo" have extremely poor living conditions, so they often express sympathy for the Volunteer Army, firing blank shots into the sky during battles, called "friend shots." The Volunteer Army also uses the slogan "Chinese people do not fight Chinese people" as a standard and does not attack them, and often obtains supplies of weapons and ammunition from them. The Volunteer Army is currently in an extremely difficult situation, but it is struggling hard and will not be eliminated for the time being. At present, the Volunteer Army has two major hopes: (1) Compatriots across the country within the customs will unite and participate in the war with the Japanese-Manchu and provide the Volunteer Army with material and spiritual assistance; (2) It is hoped that the whole country will unite and urge the government to start a war in the shortest possible time. Then not only will the Volunteer Army be an invincible force, but also most of the troops of the puppet "Manchukuo" will inevitably revolt and return to the right path. After this gentleman finished his report, warm applause shook the roof tiles and lasted for a long time. Amid this continuous applause, Professor Zhang Dongsun took the stage to speak, followed by Professor Wu Juexian. The two said nothing more than to encourage the students, but Zhang, in his speech, had the sentence "We must have a long-term detailed plan," which caused a stir among the audience, and some stood up and shouted "Wrong." This point shows that everyone is tired of hearing the terms "long-term" and "detailed "plan." Zhang simply touched on it unintentionally. Wu's speech was quite enthusiastic and won a lot of applause, but it was just the usual popular saying, with no great special features. After the speeches, an item that was originally "free speeches" was temporarily canceled by the presidium on the grounds that "the time was too late." After this, the representative of the Beiping Student National Salvation Federation reported on the future trends of the Beiping student movement. First, it was said that the Student Federation had decided that there are three core tasks in the future: (1) To protect more than 100,000 young people studying in North China; (2) To protect the safety of the cultural and educational circles in North China; (3) To retain the loyal and brave Twenty-Ninth Army in North China. Furthermore, the Student Federation organization in the future should abide by four principles: (1) To be built on the two points of "saving the country without forgetting to study" and "studying without forgetting to save the country"; (2) It should strive to cooperate with teachers and leaders from all walks of life in the school and society during its creation; (3) All activities should be carried out in an extremely democratic and open manner; (4) The representatives of each school attending the Student Federation should be directly responsible to the students of their respective schools, directly elected by the students, and directly impeached, and no longer be selected and dispatched by the student union. After the report, four resolutions were passed: (1) In the name of the meeting, a telegram should be sent to the whole country, asking the government to publicly negotiate with Japan on the Chengdu and Beihai cases; (2) In the name of the meeting, a telegram should be sent to the whole country, asking the government to strictly abide by the resolutions of the Second Plenary Session of the Central Committee and defend Suidong and North China; (3) In the name of the meeting, the Student Federation should be advised to organize a support association for the Northeast Volunteer Army; (4) In the name of the meeting, a telegram should be sent to the Northeast Army to go north and resist ×.

After the resolutions were passed, it was around six o'clock, and the meeting was adjourned. The authorities here, in order to ensure safety, continued to be on alert for one day on the 19th, which can also be said to be the aftermath of "September 18th."

Bankers Association Hosted Liang Yesterday

Those present included Pan Jiufen, Deputy Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Bank of China; Zhang Peishen, Manager of the Business Department of the Bank of Communications; Xu Xinliu, General Manager of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank; Li Fusun, General Manager of the Zhejiang Commercial Bank; Yang J眉imei, Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Shanghai Bank; Hu Xixian, Manager of the Siming Bank; Qu Jigang, Manager of the Guohua Bank; Wang Zhixin, Manager of the Xinhua Bank; Wu Yunzhai, Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Jin Cheng Bank; Zhu Boquan, Manager of the Bankers' Joint Reserve Committee; and Lin Kanghou, Secretary-General of the Bankers Association.

Opinions Expressed in Hopes of Adoption

During the banquet, Wu Yunzhai, Lin Kanghou, and others first presented their opinions on the income tax on securities and deposit interest, hoping that the government would adopt them: (1) Banks close their accounts at the end of June and the end of December. If the tax is levied from October 1st, it would be necessary to close the accounts again at the end of September. Due to the tight schedule, practical preparations may be insufficient. It is proposed to postpone it to January 1st of next year and levy it simultaneously with other income taxes. (2) Regarding the issue of levying income tax on foreign nationals and foreign banks, if the issue of foreign nationals is not resolved, deposits from foreigners at banks such as the Bank of Communications will inevitably be evaded. If the issue of foreign banks is not resolved, deposits from Chinese may also be evaded. It is hoped that the government will find a way to resolve it. (3) In terms of procedures for levying income tax on deposit interest, efforts should be made to improve the procedures and avoid double taxation, such as deposits between banks, etc.

Liang Accepted and Promised to Forward to the Ministry of Finance

Liang Hejun then replied that income taxes on public officials' salaries and income from securities and deposit interest are scheduled to be levied on October 1st and the order has already been issued to implement it as scheduled. The request to postpone it to January 1st of next year for simultaneous implementation with other income taxes seems difficult to grant. Regarding the collection of income tax from foreign nationals and foreign banks, formal notes have already been sent to various countries. The collection of income tax is handled equally for both Chinese and foreigners, and efforts will be made to improve the procedures. He promised to forward the points raised by the banks to the Ministry of Finance for consideration. At the same time, he hoped that they would understand the government's collection of income tax and assist in its implementation. The banks expressed their unanimous support for the income tax. The meeting adjourned at around 2:00 PM.

In response to the issue of levying income tax on securities and deposit interest, the Shanghai Money Trade Association, in addition to distributing the matter to its members for research and seeking opinions, also resolved at the autumn managers' meeting to organize an Income Tax Research Committee. The committee will compile and study the opinions of various firms. Three Banks and Postal Remittance Bureau to Collect on Behalf

After arriving in Shanghai from Nanjing, Liang Hejun (Jingchun), Deputy Director of the Central Direct Tax Preparatory Office, immediately contacted the Central Bank, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau to discuss the collection of income tax on securities and deposit interest. An agreement has been reached for each collecting agency to open an account and, following the methods for collecting other national taxes, sign collection contracts with the three banks and the Postal Remittance Bureau. The three banks and the Postal Remittance Bureau have now notified their branches and offices nationwide to comply with the procedures. The collection method adopts a reporting system, whereby each bank will voluntarily report its income from securities and deposit interest, and the government will then conduct random audits of each bank's books based on the reported figures.

Insurance Industry Presents to the Legislative Yuan, Appealing for Exemption from Income Tax, Citing European and American Precedents, Three Reasons Given 79

According to the Shenshi News Agency, with the Provisional Income Tax Regulations about to take effect, and because the regulations do not clearly specify whether insurance premiums and insurance payouts should be exempt from income tax, the Shanghai Insurance Industry Association recently presented its reasons to the Legislative Yuan, requesting amendments to stipulate that insurance premiums and insurance payouts for life insurance and various other types of insurance should be exempt from income tax, in order to encourage insurance. Excerpts of their appeal are as follows:

Three Reasons

(1) Article 2, Paragraph 1 of the Provisional Regulations states that income of legal entities not for profit is exempt from income tax. Those who purchase life insurance do not do so for profit. Even if the beneficiary is an individual, life insurance is relied upon to solve all important problems such as poverty, old age, dependence, illness, unemployment, lack of education, and charity. Therefore, the nature of income from life insurance and the function it serves in society are no different from the income of legal entities not for profit. This is the first reason why life insurance should be exempt from income tax. (2) Article 2, Paragraph 2, Category 2 of the Provisional Regulations states that pensions, retirement funds, and alimony for disabled workers and those unable to support themselves are exempt from income tax. Life insurance covers all matters listed in (卯). Why should general pensions, retirement funds, and alimony be exempt from tax, while insurance payouts used for pensions, retirement, and alimony, and insurance premiums set aside for pensions, retirement, and alimony, not be explicitly listed as tax-exempt? This is the second reason why life insurance should be exempt from income tax. (3) Article 2, Paragraph 3, Category 3 of the Provisional Regulations states that statutory savings of public servants and workers are exempt from income tax. The intent of this provision is to encourage thrift and make them practice saving to prepare for unforeseen circumstances. The statutory savings of public servants are encouraged and enjoy tax-exempt treatment, while insurance premiums used by ordinary citizens to prepare for unforeseen circumstances are not considered for tax exemption as an incentive. Why is it that some citizens are treated favorably while others are treated less favorably? This is the third reason why life insurance should be exempt from income tax.

European and American Precedents

Various European and American countries have precedents for exempting life insurance and various other types of insurance from income tax, either exempting insurance premiums, exempting insurance payouts, exempting entirely, or imposing certain restrictions. All of these are based on consideration of national conditions and determination of the scope of exemption. For example: (1) United States: According to Section 213(b)(1)(2)(6) of the current U.S. Income Tax Law, the following items are exempt from income tax: A. Life insurance payouts received due to death; B. Savings insurance payouts or annuities received upon maturity of the insurance, but if the income exceeds the total insurance premiums paid, income tax is levied on the excess; C. Workers' compensation or accident and health insurance payouts received due to injury. (2) United Kingdom: According to the U.K. Income Tax Act, the following items are exempt from income tax: A. Insurance premiums paid by taxpayers with an annual income of less than £1,000, not exceeding 15% of the taxable amount; B. Insurance premiums paid for life insurance, not exceeding 7% of the insurance amount; C. Deferred annuity insurance premiums paid by the taxpayer or their spouse, not exceeding £100; D. The total amount of insurance premiums not exceeding one-sixth of the income. (3) Japan: According to Article 16, Paragraph 3(6) of the current Japanese Income Tax Law, "When an insurance contract is concluded with the policyholder himself, his family, or his heir as the beneficiary of the insurance payout, the payment of insurance premiums is limited to an annual amount of 200 yen, and upon application by the policyholder, it may be deducted from the income and is not subject to income tax." (4) Germany: According to the current German Income Tax Law, insurance premiums for various types of insurance are exempt from income tax, but limited to 8,000 marks. (5) France: France had previously stipulated in its 1925 budget a very small tax on insurance premiums, collecting 0.01 centimes per 1,000 francs. However, life insurance premiums are now exempt from income tax.

True Cholera Spared This Year; Dysentery and Typhoid Fever Are Quite Rampant; Expanded Prevention of Summer Epidemics 80

Shanghai Temporary Office for Cholera Prevention Public Notice No. 3, recorded as follows, should be good news for those who care about national public health.

(1) More than two months have passed since the last public notice was issued. During this time, close attention has been paid to patients with gastrointestinal illnesses admitted to various hospitals. However, no true cholera has occurred in this port or other ports. It seems unlikely that there will be an epidemic this year.

(2) Many health experts speculated that this year would be a cholera year, but fortunately it has not occurred. Therefore, it can be said that there has been no cholera for four years (except for a few sporadic cases in the 23rd year). The good results are due to increased public awareness of hygiene, more widespread water supply, effective publicity by municipal authorities and health agencies, a reduction in diseases in neighboring areas, and the implementation of widespread anti-cholera vaccinations.

(3) In addition, there are two points that we must mention: (A) The importance of cooperation and health promotion; (B) The elimination of the concept that Shanghai is a cholera-stricken area.

(4) From the examinations of the chemical testing chamber, it is clear that human carriers do not play an important role in the spread of cholera. On the contrary, healthy carriers are most dangerous in the case of typhoid fever.

(5) The summers of the 24th and 25th years of the Republic were very hot (reaching a maximum of 100.8 degrees Fahrenheit) and the humidity was also very high. As for the summer of the 23rd year, the temperature was as high as 104.4 degrees, but the humidity was relatively low. According to Indian experience, the climate of the 25th year was indeed suitable for the occurrence of cholera. But fortunately, this infectious disease was not seen in China at all.

(6) Although no cholera has been found in Shanghai and other ports, dysentery and typhoid fever are very prevalent, especially typhoid fever. The mortality rate of this disease is very high in Shanghai, Shantou, Xiamen, Guangzhou, and other places. The following are the cases in Shanghai in the 24th and 25th years:

Typhoid Fever Dysentery

Cases Deaths Cases Deaths

24th Year 424 302 406 75

25th Year 664 316 449 78

Chinese troops have been forced to receive anti-typhoid vaccinations, and very few have contracted the disease, which proves the value of the vaccination.

(7) The following is a list of the number of anti-cholera vaccinations provided by various health agencies in Shanghai. The total number of vaccinations last year was 767,725.

(8) This is the final public notice of this year. The Temporary Office for Cholera Prevention is deeply grateful for the efforts and assistance of various municipal health agencies and other organizations. Without cooperation, the work of this office could not have progressed. Since the anti-cholera movement has been so successful, it seems that expanding this work to other intestinal diseases, such as typhoid fever, dysentery, and various gastroenteritis, is also feasible. The causes and prevention methods of these infectious diseases are very similar. The results achieved in cholera can also be obtained in other intestinal diseases. This year, it is proposed to discuss the establishment of a Summer Epidemic Prevention Office to replace the current Temporary Office for Cholera Prevention, so that China and the world can have a healthy Shanghai. This is an important plan for today.

Postal and Customs Employees Should Maintain Order: Executive Yuan Orders Ministries of Transportation and Finance to Instruct Their Subordinates to Comply 92

The Executive Yuan instructed the Ministries of Transportation and Finance, stating: According to the Ministry of Military Affairs' report No. 310 on September 15, 1936, which was based on a report from Gu Zheng Lun of the Gendarmerie Headquarters, and a report from Zheng Zhi, Captain of the Gendarmerie Escorting Ships in the Wu River, Report No. 196 on August 13 of this year, it was stated that since the reorganization of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, efforts have been made to ensure passenger safety, with designated entry and exit routes for passengers boarding and disembarking each ship, which aligns with Article 1 of the Executive Yuan's Instruction No. 843 on February 8, which prohibits boarding ships without tickets, and with the New Life Movement. However, during my recent duty tour to various ports, the gendarmerie stationed at each port and escorting ships reported that customs and postal employees have not changed their old habits. They often do not follow designated routes when entering and exiting ports, walking arbitrarily, often colliding with passengers and obstructing traffic. The gendarmerie, as part of their duty, has politely dissuaded them, but they not only did not listen but became angry and unreasonable, with a strong and uncooperative attitude. It is difficult for the gendarmerie to serve due to the arrogant attitude of customs and postal employees and their refusal to heed advice. It is requested that you report to the Executive Yuan and instruct the customs and postal agencies in various ports to strictly require their employees to maintain order in port terminals to ensure passenger safety and facilitate the gendarmerie's duties, which is appropriate. Based on this, it has been found that customs personnel walking on and off ships in ports and failing to maintain order, leading to disputes with the gendarmerie providing guidance, has occurred more than once. Previously, it was reported that on July 21 of this year, when the Jianghua ship, traveling from Shanghai and stationed in Hankou, arrived in Nanjing, customs officers led five search team members and one patrol officer to investigate over ten pieces of smuggled goods. After the inspection was completed, they disembarked from the entrance, and the gendarmerie, seeing that it violated the regulations of the China Merchants Bureau and the New Life Movement, advised them to use the designated entry and exit routes, but the customs officers, relying on their power, refused to listen, leading to a dispute. On July 21 of the same year, when the Jiangshun ship sailed down to Shanghai, customs personnel did not follow the "left up, right down" route and boarded where passengers were disembarking. The gendarmerie stepped forward to dissuade them, but the customs officers refused to comply, leading to another dispute. Although it is legitimate for customs officers to perform their duties for convenience, all levels of public officials should earnestly implement regulations, especially when the China Merchants Bureau has just been reformed and the New Life Movement is being actively promoted. The captain's request is appropriate. It is appropriate to report to your office and request the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministries of Transportation and Finance to instruct the postal and customs employees in various ports to comply with the order of port terminals to maintain the New Life Movement. Based on this, it has been found that the commander's request is a factual situation and should be reported to your office for review and implementation. Based on this, it should be approved. In addition to issuing separate orders, this order requires your ministry to instruct the post offices (customs) in various ports to strictly enforce the regulations and instruct all employees to comply. This order.

Feng Shaoshan Speaks on Industry and Commerce in Various Parts of Southeast Asia (Continued from Yesterday's Newspaper) 101

Yunnan is adjacent to the capital city of Yangon, the summer government moves to Maymyo (on a high mountain, 3,340 feet above sea level, with a very cool climate). Our country has consulates, chambers of commerce, schools, guild halls, etc. in Yangon. The total population of Myanmar is 14,647,493, of which 193,594 are overseas Chinese (of the overseas Chinese in Yangon, there are 30,622). (The capital of Myanmar is Mandalay, the last of its capital cities, because the Burmese king's territory was captured by the British on November 28, 1885, and he was exiled to the coast of Mumbai, and the country perished. The most numerous overseas Chinese are Yunnanese and Fujianese, followed by Cantonese. The Yunnanese mostly deal in Sichuan yellow and white silk, jade, and other businesses, while the Fujianese mostly deal in mountain goods, grains, and so on. It is said that many Fujianese have

settled in Myanmar, opening shops in various mountain areas (i.e., villages), marrying U Tao women (i.e., Burmese women) as wives, and often lending funds to local farmers during spring plowing, to be repaid in cash or discounted grain at harvest time, at extremely high interest rates. The Taishan Cantonese mostly run taverns and pawnshops (pawnshops operate in the same way as taverns). In addition, overseas Chinese in Yangon often open shops, using small profits to absorb local indigenous funds to establish businesses and run pawnshops in the interior. Many wealthy overseas Chinese in Myanmar have also opened rice mills and machine factories. Furthermore, in my general observations in India, there is no shortage of wealthy merchants, with some individuals owning two or three large-scale hemp factories and packaging plants, or also possessing porcelain factories, light bulb factories, etc. Normally,

they store millions of goods and raw materials without relying on bank loans. The young people are also very active, and industry is gradually developing. In addition, there is a group of people in India, the Madrasis from the south, indigenous people called Jining, who specialize in labor, and another group called Meng Hua, who control the reins of commerce throughout India, and another group of Qizhi people, who specialize in lending money at high interest rates, like the Shanghai custom of having usurious loans. Currently, the national goods that our country ships to Southeast Asia are mostly daily necessities needed by overseas Chinese, occasionally shipped from Hong Kong, but they are mostly national goods produced by machine in Fujian and Guangdong. Recently, there has been some activity, such as cotton fabrics, undershirts, or leather bags. As for Tibet, which borders India, each person must have

a delicate porcelain rice bowl, which must be a Chinese product. These goods are now shipped by overseas Chinese to Kolkata, and Tibetans come to Kolkata to purchase them. Currently, for the various kinds of porcelain needed by our country, the porcelain manufacturers in Jingdezhen, Jiangxi Province, are shortsighted and do not know how to cater to other people's psychology, improve their products, and accept orders. Taking a set of teacups as an example, they sell very well in Southeast Asia, but if their style is slightly changed, no one will accept them. In my opinion, the Ministry of Industry of our country should work with the Construction Department of the Jiangxi Provincial Government to find ways to improve the goods. Recently, I heard that Du Chongyuan has been released from prison and is continuing to run the Guangda Porcelain Company. In this case, the above-mentioned things can certainly be handled by the company. I have now given a rambling report,

which has taken up a lot of time. In short, there is great hope for the promotion of national goods overseas, especially in Southeast Asia. Not only are overseas Chinese welcoming national goods, but the local indigenous people are also very welcoming. However, I hope that national goods manufacturers will constantly study the customs, climate, and habits of various parts of Southeast Asia to improve their products. For example, silk fabrics in Southeast Asia need to be especially soft and thin, because they are located in the tropics, and this is necessary. I also have some unfulfilled intentions, believing that in addition to promoting national goods abroad, we should also enable the products produced by our overseas Chinese with capital and labor to be shipped back to our country for sale, so that the economy can be revitalized. To do this, we must immediately organize an agency for import and export trade, which should be of the greatest concern to people at home and abroad.

Ministry of Finance Approves: Workbooks Do Not Require Stamps 104

The Ministry of Finance yesterday issued a reply to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce regarding the issue of stamp use, stating: I have read the song code and checked the workbooks issued by factories to workers for recording, the work reports copied by workers to factories at the end of the month, and the daily absenteeism and overtime registration forms used by factories. All are used to assess worker performance and have the same purpose as setting up sign-in, leave, and attendance books. Naturally, there is no need to use stamps. However, if there is a record of wages in the absenteeism and overtime registration form and it is compiled into a book using loose-leaf pages, it should still be handled according to the book rules.
